                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Sodium-Ion Pseudocapacitors Based on 3D Na2Ti3O7 Nanosheet Arrays/Carbon Textiles Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Shengyang; Shen, Laifa; Li, Hongsen; Pang, Gang; Dou, Hui; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible energy storage devices are crit. components for emerging flexible and wearable electronics.  Improving the electrochem. performance of flexible energy storage devices depends largely on development of novel electrode architectures and new systems.  Here, a new class of flexible energy storage device called flexible sodium-ion pseudocapacitors is developed based on 3D-flexible Na2Ti3O7 nanosheet arrays/carbon textiles (NTO/CT) as anode and flexible reduced graphene oxide film (GFs) as cathode without metal current collectors or conducting additives.  The NTO/CT anode with advanced electrode architectures is fabricated by directly growing Na2Ti3O7 nanosheet arrays on carbon textiles with robust adhesion through a simple hydrothermal process.  The flexible GF//NTO/CT configuration achieves a high energy d. of 55 Wh/kg and high power d. of 3000 W/kg.  Taking the fully packaged flexible sodium-ion pseudocapacitors into consideration, the max. practical volumetric energy d. and power d. reach up to 1.3 mWh/cm3 and 70 mW/cm3, resp.  In addn., the flexible GF//NTO/CT device demonstrates a stable electrochem. performances with almost 100% capacitance retention under harsh mech. deformation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr6t3cMbgvZfLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgvjuIIZzFmBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmsF2rtbc%253D&amp;md5=4a3dbff1205414f306d3f45ea387341b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.surfcoat.2016.06.065"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Walsh, F.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been proposed as candidates for replacing Li-ion batteries.  The authors examine the viability of Na-ion anode materials based on Na alloys or hard carbons in terms of volumetric energy d.  Due to the bigger size of the Na atom compared to the Li atom, Na alloys would lead to anode materials with about half the volumetric energy d. of their Li analogs.  Volumetric energy densities obtainable with sodiated hard carbons would also be significantly less than those obtainable with lithiated graphite.  These findings highlight the need of novel ideas for Na-ion anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfbyHmIC7uUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgvjuIIZzFmBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXpt1Ont7c%253D&amp;md5=f132981922c6ce146def4cd54c721e2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702582"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Beyond Insertion for Na-Ion Batteries: Nanostructured Alloying and Conversion Anode Materials</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent progress on sodium ion batteries: potential high-performance anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Li; Zheng, Yang; Zhang, Shilin; Yang, Jianping; Shao, Zongping; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to massively growing demand arising from energy storage systems, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been recognized as the most attractive alternative to the current commercialized lithium ion batteries (LIBs) owing to the wide availability and accessibility of sodium.  Unfortunately, the low energy d., inferior power d. and poor cycle life are still the main issues for SIBs in the current drive to push the entire technol. forward to meet the benchmark requirements for commercialization.  Over the past few years, tremendous efforts have been devoted to improving the performance of SIBs, in terms of higher energy d. and longer cycling lifespans, by optimizing the electrode structure or the electrolyte compn.  In particular, among the established anode systems, those materials, such as metals/alloys, phosphorus/phosphides, and metal oxides/sulfides/selenides, that typically deliver high theor. sodium-storage capacities have received growing interest and achieved significant progress.  Although some review articles on electrodes for SIBs have been published already, many new reports on these anode materials are constantly emerging, with more promising electrochem. performance achieved via novel structural design, surface modification, electrochem. performance testing techniques, etc.  So, we herein summarize the most recent developments on these high-performance anode materials for SIBs in this review.  Furthermore, the different reaction mechanisms, the challenges assocd. with these materials, and effective approaches to enhance performance are discussed.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly compacted TiO2/C microspheres via in-situ surface-confined intergrowth with ultra-long life for reversible Na-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Jinpeng; Yang, Haining; Kong, Weiqiang; Man, Jianzong; Zhou, Zhaoyang; Feng, Wei; Sun, Juncai; Wen, Zhongsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">582</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2 as the promising anode material candidate of sodium-ion battery suffers from poor cond. and slow ion diffusion rate, which severely hampers its development.  Highly compacted TiO2/C microspheres without inner pores/tunnels are synthesized by a very facile one-pot rapid processing method based on novel in-situ surface-confined inter-growth mechanism.  This highly compacted TiO2/C microspheres exhibit an excellent electrochem. performance of reversible Na+ storage despite with relatively large particle/aggregation size from submicrometer to micrometer.  An outstanding cycling stability extending to 10,000 cycles is gained with a high retention capacity of 140.5 mA-h g-1 at a current rate of 2 A g-1.  An ultra-high reversible capacity of 362 mA-h g-1 close to its theoretic specific capacity is obtained at a current rate of 0.05 A g-1.  The successful combination of highly compacted structure with large particle size, excellent electrochem. performance as well as rapid cost-effective prepg. process might provide a potential industrial approach for efficiently synthesizing electrode materials for Na ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKhUoylUciz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6vY8acnJk3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslyjurzJ&amp;md5=ceffacaafe864e5fa49d0a7f4cd66ee1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta00041b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cha, H.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase TiO2: Better Anode Material Than Amorphous and Rutile Phases of TiO2 for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Dou, Shixue; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous TiO2@C nanospheres were synthesized via a template approach.  After being sintered under different conditions, two types of polyphase TiO2 hollow nanospheres were obtained.  The electrochem. properties of the amorphous TiO2 nanospheres and the TiO2 hollow nanospheres with different phases were characterized as anodes for the Na-ion batteries.  It was found that all the samples demonstrated excellent cyclability, which was sustainable for hundreds of cycles with little capacity fading, although the anatase TiO2 presented a capability that was better than that of the mixed anatase/rutile TiO2 or the amorphous TiO2@C.  Through crystallog. anal., it was revealed that the anatase TiO2 crystal structure supplies two-dimensional diffusion paths for Na-ion intercalation and more accommodation sites.  D. functional theory calcns. indicated lower energy barriers for the insertion of Na+ into anatase TiO2.  Therefore, anatase TiO2 hollow nanospheres show excellent high-rate performance.  Through ex situ field emission SEM, it was revealed that the TiO2 hollow nanosphere architecture can be maintained for hundreds of cycles, which is the main reason for its superior cyclability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohsYIdXKQ-ZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6vY8acnJk3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlSmtLvO&amp;md5=4e702bfdd0ada6787dd1d1f2bf052430</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.11.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur Doped Ultra-Thin Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets/Graphene Nanocomposite for High-Performance Pseudocapacitive Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">37</span>â <span class="NLM_lpage">43</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To enhance the intrinsic elec. conductivities of TiO2(B) nanobelts, nitrogen(N)-doped TiO2(B) nanobelts (N-TNB) were prepd. in this study by a facile and cost-effective hydrothermal method using urea as the nitrogen source with TiO2 (P25) nanoparticles. XPS confirmed that the N-atoms preferentially occupied up to ~ 0.516 atom% in the interstitial sites of the N-TNB and the max. concn. of substituted-N bonds in the N-TNB was ~ 0.154 atom%, thereby the total concn. of doped nitrogen elements of ~ 0.67 atom% improved the high intrinsic elec. cond. and ionic diffusivity of the TiO2(B) nanobelts.  The as-prepd. N-TNB electrode delivered the highest specific capacity of 133.9 mAh g-1 in the first cycle, with an exceptional cyclic capacity retention at an ultrafast current rate of 1000 mA g-1 ; this is not less than 51% after 500 cycles and represents an excellent rate capability of ~ 37 mAh g-1 at an ultra-high rate of 40 C.  These values are among the best ever reported on comparison of the delivered highest discharge capacity of N-TNB at 1000 mA g-1 and high-rate capabilities of its Li+ ion storage with the literature data for N-TNB (~ 231.5 mAh g-1 at a very low c.d. of 16.75 mA g-1, ~ 0.1 C) of similar materials used in sodium-ion batteries.  This implies the potential feasibility of these N-TNB as high-capacity anode materials for next-generation, high-energy-d., electrochem. energy-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6g6_ZYV9QH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6vY8acnJk3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVSnsbbK&amp;md5=1aca4538c21d2960f54846c375242c67</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b14597"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur-Doped TiO<sub>2</sub> Anchored on a Large-Area Carbon Sheet as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Anchored on a Large-Area Carbon Sheet as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yan; He, Xinrui; Tang, Jiahui; Jiang, Jing; Ji, Xiaobo; Wang, Chao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen vacancies enhance pseudocapacitive charge storage properties of MoO3-x</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyung-Seok; Cook, John B.; Lin, Hao; Ko, Jesse S.; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Ozolins, Vidvuds; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The short charging times and high power capabilities assocd. with capacitive energy storage make this approach an attractive alternative to batteries.  One limitation of electrochem. capacitors is their low energy d. and for this reason, there is widespread interest in pseudocapacitive materials that use Faradaic reactions to store charge.  One candidate pseudocapacitive material is orthorhombic MoO3 (Î±-MoO3), a layered compd. with a high theor. capacity for lithium (279 mA h g-1 or 1,005 C g-1).  Here, we report on the properties of reduced Î±-MoO3-x(R-MoO3-x) and compare it with fully oxidized Î±-MoO3 (F-MoO3).  The introduction of oxygen vacancies leads to a larger interlayer spacing that promotes faster charge storage kinetics and enables the Î±-MoO3 structure to be retained during the insertion and removal of Li ions.  The higher specific capacity of the R-MoO3-x is attributed to the reversible formation of a significant amt. of Mo4+ following lithiation.  This study underscores the potential importance of incorporating oxygen vacancies into transition metal oxides as a strategy for increasing the charge storage kinetics of redox-active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9QgRHEtnVrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw_MFIS6XFxQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MXene-derived TiO2/reduced graphene oxide composite with an enhanced capacitive capacity for Li-ion and K-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang, Yongzheng; Hu, Rong; Liu, Boya; Zhang, Yingying; Zhu, Kai; Yan, Jun; Ye, Ke; Cheng, Kui; Wang, Guiling; Cao, Dianxue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-ion and K-ion batteries present their unique advantages of high energy d. and low cost, resp. Herein, a two-dimensional TiO2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composite was prepd. by a facile hydrothermal method.  TiO2 nanoparticles are transformed from Ti2C MXene and connect the RGO nanosheets to form a sheet-like structure.  Serving as the anode material, the TiO2/RGO presents high capacity, remarkable rate ability and long cycling performance for both Li- and K-ion batteries.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Defect-assisted selective surface phosphorus doping to enhance rate capability of titanium dioxide for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; He, Hanna; Zhu, Youhuan; Wang, Zhenyu; Qin, Ning; Gu, Shuai; Li, Zhiqiang; Luo, Wen; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doping is an effective strategy to simultaneously improve the electronic cond. and regulate the ionic diffusion kinetics of TiO2 being considered as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  However, efficient phosphorus doping at high concn. in well-crystd. TiO2 nanoparticles is still a big challenge.  Herein, the authors propose a defect-assisted phosphorus doping strategy to selectively engineer the surface structure of TiO2 nanoparticles.  The reduced TiO2-x shell layer that is rich in oxygen defects and Ti3+ species precisely triggered a high concn. of phosphorus doping (â¼7.8 at.%), and consequently a TiO2@TiO2-x-P core@shell architecture was produced.  Comprehensive characterizations and first-principle calcns. proved that the surface-functionalized TiO2-x-P thin layer endowed the TiO2@TiO2-x-P with substantially enhanced electronic cond. and accelerated Na ion transportation, resulting in great rate capability (167 mA h g-1 at 10 000 mA g-1) and stable cycling (99% after 5000 cycles at 10 A g-1).  Combining in/ex situ x-ray diffraction with ex situ ESR clearly demonstrated the high reversibility and robust mech. behavior of TiO2@TiO2-x-P upon long-term cycling.  This work provides an interesting and effective strategy for precise heteroatoms doping to improve the electrochem. performance of nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV2X3aWTMl9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw_MFIS6XFxQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVamtb7P&amp;md5=cd8e232f3259e7881601dbcf23b2e6ee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.8b06540"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yeh, H.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tai, S.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hsieh, C.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2 has attracted considerable attention as a potential alternative anode material in Li-ion rechargeable batteries.  In recent years, the incorporation of O vacancy into such anode materials was demonstrated to improve elec. cond., cycling stability, and rate performance through exptl. studies.  Li intercalation and diffusion behavior in pristine and O-defective TiO2 were studied by 1st principles based on d. functional theory calcns.  Total energies of possible intercalation sites were 1st calcd. to find the most favorable site in the three commonly used polymorphs: anatase, rutile, and TiO2(B).  Also, the energy barriers of possible paths for Li diffusion from one stable site to another were calcd. by the climbing image nudged elastic band method.  The electronic structures are also presented to compare conductivities of pristine and O-defective TiO2.  The authors' results indicate that although all three phases show enhanced cond. via O-defect introduction, TiO2(B) is the best choice for Li intercalation and diffusion as potential anode materials, having the lowest intercalation energy and Li diffusion barrier, both of which are expected to result in better battery performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9S_jQlhpOkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw_MFIS6XFxQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The rate-detg. process for electrochem. energy storage is largely detd. by ion transport occurring in the electrode materials.  Apart from decreasing the distance of ion diffusion, the enhancement of ionic mobility is crucial for ion transport.  Here, a localized electron enhanced ion transport mechanism to promote ion mobility for ultrafast energy storage is proposed.  Theor. calcns. and anal. reveal that highly localized electrons can be induced by intrinsic defects, and the migration barrier of ions can be obviously reduced.  Consistently, expt. results reveal that this mechanism leads to an enhancement of Li/Na ion diffusivity by two orders of magnitude.         </div><div class="casAbstract">K is an earth abundant alternative to Li for rechargeable batteries, but a crit. limitation in K ion battery anodes is the low capacity of KC8 graphite intercalation compds. in comparison to conventional LiC6.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium/Potassium-Ion Batteries: Boosting the Rate Capability and Cycle Life by Combining Morphology, Defect and Structure Engineering</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Huijuan; Xu, Rui; Feng, Yuezhan; Zeng, Sifan; Jiang, Yu; Wang, Huijuan; Luo, Wei; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based materials have been considered as the most promising anode materials for both sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs), owing to their good chem. stability, high elec. cond., and environmental benignity.  However, due to the large sizes of sodium and potassium ions, it is a great challenge to realize a carbon anode with high reversible capacity, long cycle life, and high rate capability.  Herein, by rational design, N-doped 3D mesoporous carbon nanosheets (N-CNS) are successfully synthesized, which can realize unprecedented electrochem. performance for both SIBs and PIBs.  The N-CNS possess an ultrathin nanosheet structure with hierarchical pores, ultrahigh level of pyridinic N/pyrrolic N, and an expanded interlayer distance.  The beneficial features that can enhance the Na-/K-ion intercalation/deintercalation kinetic process, shorten the diffusion length for both ions and electrons, and accommodate the vol. change are demonstrated.  Hence, the N-CNS-based electrode delivers a high capacity of 239 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 10 000 cycles for SIBs and 321 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 5000 cycles for PIBs.  First-principles calcn. shows that the ultrahigh doping level of pyridinic N/pyrrolic N contributes to the enhanced sodium and potassium storage performance by modulating the charge d. distribution on the carbon surface.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVG-cQvHto_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljo4Ch9dcTPNg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pinecone-like hierarchical anatase TiO2 bonded with carbon enabling ultrahigh cycling rates for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jun; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhang, Yan; Huang, Zhaodong; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical anatase TiO2 homogeneously tuned by using carbon through Ti-C bonds has been designed, exploiting carbon quantum dots as uniform carbon additives and functionalization inducers for structure tailoring and surface modification.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black Anatase Titania with Ultrafast Sodium-Storage Performances Stimulated by Oxygen Vacancies</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jun; Ding, Zhiying; Wang, Chao; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhang, Yan; Wang, Chiwei; Zou, Guoqiang; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructured black anatase titania with oxygen vacancies (OVs) is efficiently obtained and employed as an anode in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) for the first time.  The incorporation of OVs into TiO2 is demonstrated to render considerably enhanced-rate performances, higher initial capacities, and an accelerated electrochem. activation process during cycling, derived from the boosted intrinsic elec. cond. and improved kinetics of Na uptake.  Bestowed with the integrated merits of OVs and shortened Na ion diffusion length in the nanostructure, black titania delivers a reversible specific capacity of 207.6 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, retains 99.1% over 500 cycles at 1 C stably, and still maintains 91.2 mAh g-1 even at the high rate of 20 C.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The surface science of titanium dioxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Diebold, Ulrike</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Surface Science Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2003</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5-8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">53-229</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSREDI</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  TiO2 is the most investigated single-cryst. system in the surface science of metal oxides, and the literature on rutile (1 1 0), (1 0 0), (0 0 1), and anatase surfaces is discussed.  This paper starts with a summary of the wide variety of tech. fields where TiO2 is of importance.  The bulk structure and bulk defects (as far as relevant to the surface properties) are briefly reviewed.  Rules to predict stable oxide surfaces are exemplified on rutile (1 1 0).  The surface structure of rutile (1 1 0) is discussed in some detail.  Theor. predicted and exptl. detd. relaxations of surface geometries are compared, and defects (step edge orientations, point and line defects, impurities, surface manifestations of crystallog. shear planes-CSPs) are discussed, as well as the image contrast in scanning tunneling microscopy (STM).  The controversy about the correct model for the (1Ã2) reconstruction appears to be settled.  Different surface prepn. methods, such as reoxidn. of reduced crystals, can cause a drastic effect on surface geometries and morphol., and recommendations for prepg. different TiO2(1 1 0) surfaces are given.  The structure of the TiO2(1 0 0)-(1Ã1) surface is discussed and the proposed models for the (1Ã3) reconstruction are critically reviewed.  Very recent results on anatase (1 0 0) and (1 0 1) surfaces are included.  The electronic structure of stoichiometric TiO2 surfaces is now well understood.  Surface defects can be detected with a variety of surface spectroscopies.  The vibrational structure is dominated by strong Fuchs-Kliewer phonons, and high-resoln. electron energy loss spectra often need to be deconvoluted to render useful information about adsorbed mols.  The growth of metals (Li, Na, K, Cs, Ca, Al, Ti, V, Nb, Cr, Mo, Mn, Fe, Co, Rh, Ir, Ni, Pd, Pt, Cu, Ag, Au) as well as some metal oxides on TiO2 is reviewed.  The tendency to wet' the overlayer, the growth morphol., the epitaxial relationship, and the strength of the interfacial oxidn./redn. reaction all follow clear trends across the periodic table, with the reactivity of the overlayer metal towards O being the most decisive factor.  Alkali atoms form ordered superstructures at low coverages.  Recent progress in understanding the surface structure of metals in the strong-metal support interaction' (SMSI) state is summarized.Literature is reviewed on the adsorption and reaction of a wide variety of inorg. mols. (H2, O2, H2O, CO, CO2, N2, NH3, NOx, sulfur- and halogen-contg. mols., rare gases) as well as org. mols. (carboxylic acids, alcs., aldehydes and ketones, alkynes, pyridine and its derivates, silanes, Me halides).  The application of TiO2-based systems in photo-active devices is discussed, and the results on UHV-based photocatalytic studies are summarized.  The review ends with a brief conclusion and outlook of TiO2-based surface science for the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3ORpC9Y7lsbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRMJ6t4YTWNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3sXivVWqtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=105db7a87a360e2042de551c7a4a05fc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/d0cc03099f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability of Dual-Ion Batteries Enabled by TiO<sub>2</sub> Microspheres with Abundant Oxygen Vacancies</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Pseudocapacitance Boosts Ultrafast, High-Capacity Sodium Storage of 3D Graphene Foam-Encapsulated TiO2 Architecture</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Rui; Ma, Yitian; Qu, Wenjie; Qian, Ji; Li, Li; Wu, Feng; Chen, RenJie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is an attractive anode for Li-ion batteries and Na-ion batteries because of its structural stability.  However, the electrochem. capability of anatase TiO2 is unsatisfactory due to its intrinsically low elec. cond. and poor ion diffusivity at the electrode/electrolyte interface.  We prepd. 3D lightwt. graphene aerogel-encapsulated anatase TiO2, which exhibits a high reversible capacity (390 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), a superior rate performance (164.9 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1), and a long-term cycling capability (capacity retention of 86.8% after 7800 cycles).  The major energy-storage mechanism is surface capacitance dominated, which favors a high capacity and fast Na+ uptake.  The inherent features of 3D porous aerogels provide addnl. active reaction sites and facilitate fast charge diffusion and easy ion access.  This will enable the development of 3D interconnected, graphene-based, high-capacity active materials for the development of next-generation energy-storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoA9imc5cibIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRMJ6t4YTWNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosF2ntbo%253D&amp;md5=ff018a44946f3129ecf1da2a84ec5b86</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Augustyn, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Come, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lowe, M.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2Â·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 Î¼m thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRMJ6t4YTWNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nanosheets Constructed by Graphene-Coated, Interconnected TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAdnMS9JrSwg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c9ta09643d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doped CoSb@C Nanofibers as a Self-Supporting Anode for High-Performance K-Ion and Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-doped CoSb@C nanofibers as a self-supporting anode for high-performance K-ion and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Jun; Zhu, Kunjie; Liu, Pei; Si, Yuchang; Chai, Yujun; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, the prepn. of CoSb nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanofibers with a raised surface (N-doped CoSb@C nanofibers) via the electrospinning method is reported for the first time.  The distinct structure facilitates the pseudocapacitive behaviors, which is the key to obtain fast kinetics and long cyclability.  N and Co elements can not only optimize the electronic configuration but also buffer the vol. changes of the material during cycling.  For potassium-ion batteries, the capacity maintains 250 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1, and for sodium-ion batteries, the capacity keeps 413 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Thus, this work makes a great contribution towards exploring high-capacity anodes for practical potassium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQKX1IpNRVY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAdnMS9JrSwg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFymsb%252FF&amp;md5=a0a468cd018aa0125c2daa9ff77dfbc4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.34133/2019/6930294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Superior Rate Performances Coexisting in Carbon-Based Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>Research</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2019</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6930294</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High capacity and superior rate performances coexisting in carbon-based sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yuqian; Zhang, Liyuan; Wang, Xiuli; Xia, Xinhui; Xie, Dong; Gu, Changdong; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Research (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous carbon is considered as a prospective and serviceable anode for the storage of sodium.  In this contribution, we illuminate the transformation rule of defect/void ratio and the restrictive relation between specifc capacity and rate capability.  Inspired by this mechanism, ratio of plateau/slope capacity is regulated via temp.-control pyrolysis.  Moreover, pore-forming reaction is induced to create defects, open up the isolated voids, and build fast ion channels to further enhance the capacity and rate ability.  Numerous fast ion channels, high ion-electron cond., and abundant defects lead the designed porous hard carbon/Co3O4 anode to realize a high specifc capacity, prolonged circulation ability, and enhanced capacity at high rates.  Tis research deepens the comprehension of sodium storage behavior and proposes a fabrication approach to achieve high performance carbonaceous anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_0VZqb8c_ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAdnMS9JrSwg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Sgs7vM&amp;md5=bc3a9393d804c3271239d5cfd700fb90</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-storage behavior of electron-rich element-doped amorphous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yuqian; Zhang, Liyuan; Wang, Xiuli; Xia, Xinhui; Xie, Dong; Gu, Changdong; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Physics Reviews</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In recent years, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been widely investigated due to limited lithium resources.  Hence, it is of great importance to develop suitable anodes for SIBs.  In recent works, doped amorphous carbon has been considered a prospective and serviceable anode for the storage of sodium.  In this study, sodium-storage behavior in electron-rich, element-modified, amorphous carbon is addressed, considering N and P.  The affinity of N-doped amorphous carbon is identified by calcg. the electron distributions of the N-doped structures.  Furthermore, the adsorption energies of sodium in the P-doped amorphous carbon systems are analyzed to elucidate the storage behavior of doping.  From the above anal., the internal structure of co-doped carbon is characterized and pyrrolic N and P-O structures reveal excellent sodium-storage performance.  Consequently, hydrothermal treatment is designed to build the precursor of the required P-O structure.  Based on the sodium-storage theory, a carbon anode doped with dual electron-rich elements is synthesized successfully, which shows enhanced electrochem. performances in terms of cycle life and capacity in batteries.  As a result, these research results fill the theor. gap of the sodium-storage behavior of electron-rich, element-doped, amorphous carbon and provide the exptl. basis for its application. Due to the bigger size of the Na atom compared to the Li atom, Na alloys would lead to anode materials with about half the volumetric energy d. of their Li analogs.  Volumetric energy densities obtainable with sodiated hard carbons would also be significantly less than those obtainable with lithiated graphite.  These findings highlight the need of novel ideas for Na-ion anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfbyHmIC7uUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKJlTLuqK5Lw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXpt1Ont7c%253D&amp;md5=f132981922c6ce146def4cd54c721e2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702582"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Beyond Insertion for Na-Ion Batteries: Nanostructured Alloying and Conversion Anode Materials</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to massively growing demand arising from energy storage systems, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been recognized as the most attractive alternative to the current commercialized lithium ion batteries (LIBs) owing to the wide availability and accessibility of sodium.  Unfortunately, the low energy d., inferior power d. and poor cycle life are still the main issues for SIBs in the current drive to push the entire technol. forward to meet the benchmark requirements for commercialization.  Over the past few years, tremendous efforts have been devoted to improving the performance of SIBs, in terms of higher energy d. and longer cycling lifespans, by optimizing the electrode structure or the electrolyte compn.  In particular, among the established anode systems, those materials, such as metals/alloys, phosphorus/phosphides, and metal oxides/sulfides/selenides, that typically deliver high theor. sodium-storage capacities have received growing interest and achieved significant progress.  Although some review articles on electrodes for SIBs have been published already, many new reports on these anode materials are constantly emerging, with more promising electrochem. performance achieved via novel structural design, surface modification, electrochem. performance testing techniques, etc.  So, we herein summarize the most recent developments on these high-performance anode materials for SIBs in this review.  Furthermore, the different reaction mechanisms, the challenges assocd. with these materials, and effective approaches to enhance performance are discussed.         </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2 as the promising anode material candidate of sodium-ion battery suffers from poor cond. and slow ion diffusion rate, which severely hampers its development.  Highly compacted TiO2/C microspheres without inner pores/tunnels are synthesized by a very facile one-pot rapid processing method based on novel in-situ surface-confined inter-growth mechanism.  This highly compacted TiO2/C microspheres exhibit an excellent electrochem. performance of reversible Na+ storage despite with relatively large particle/aggregation size from submicrometer to micrometer.  An outstanding cycling stability extending to 10,000 cycles is gained with a high retention capacity of 140.5 mA-h g-1 at a current rate of 2 A g-1.  An ultra-high reversible capacity of 362 mA-h g-1 close to its theoretic specific capacity is obtained at a current rate of 0.05 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous TiO2@C nanospheres were synthesized via a template approach.  After being sintered under different conditions, two types of polyphase TiO2 hollow nanospheres were obtained.  The electrochem. properties of the amorphous TiO2 nanospheres and the TiO2 hollow nanospheres with different phases were characterized as anodes for the Na-ion batteries.  It was found that all the samples demonstrated excellent cyclability, which was sustainable for hundreds of cycles with little capacity fading, although the anatase TiO2 presented a capability that was better than that of the mixed anatase/rutile TiO2 or the amorphous TiO2@C.  Through crystallog. anal., it was revealed that the anatase TiO2 crystal structure supplies two-dimensional diffusion paths for Na-ion intercalation and more accommodation sites.  D. functional theory calcns. indicated lower energy barriers for the insertion of Na+ into anatase TiO2.  Therefore, anatase TiO2 hollow nanospheres show excellent high-rate performance.                 10.1088/1361-6528/ab9fb6</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped TiO2 (B) nanobelts enabling enhancement of electronic conductivity and efficiency of lithium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Nangyeong; Raj, Michael Ruby; Lee, Gibaek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">415401</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To enhance the intrinsic elec. conductivities of TiO2(B) nanobelts, nitrogen(N)-doped TiO2(B) nanobelts (N-TNB) were prepd. in this study by a facile and cost-effective hydrothermal method using urea as the nitrogen source with TiO2 (P25) nanoparticles. XPS confirmed that the N-atoms preferentially occupied up to ~ 0.516 atom% in the interstitial sites of the N-TNB and the max. concn. of substituted-N bonds in the N-TNB was ~ 0.154 atom%, thereby the total concn. of doped nitrogen elements of ~ 0.67 atom% improved the high intrinsic elec. cond. and ionic diffusivity of the TiO2(B) nanobelts.  The as-prepd. N-TNB electrode delivered the highest specific capacity of 133.9 mAh g-1 in the first cycle, with an exceptional cyclic capacity retention at an ultrafast current rate of 1000 mA g-1 ; this is not less than 51% after 500 cycles and represents an excellent rate capability of ~ 37 mAh g-1 at an ultra-high rate of 40 C.  These values are among the best ever reported on comparison of the delivered highest discharge capacity of N-TNB at 1000 mA g-1 and high-rate capabilities of its Li+ ion storage with the literature data for N-TNB (~ 231.5 mAh g-1 at a very low c.d. of 16.75 mA g-1, ~ 0.1 C) of similar materials used in sodium-ion batteries.  This implies the potential feasibility of these N-TNB as high-capacity anode materials for next-generation, high-energy-d., electrochem. energy-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6g6_ZYV9QH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljnbLC1cLYUKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVSnsbbK&amp;md5=1aca4538c21d2960f54846c375242c67</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b14597"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur-Doped TiO<sub>2</sub> Anchored on a Large-Area Carbon Sheet as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl. The authors' results indicate that although all three phases show enhanced cond. via O-defect introduction, TiO2(B) is the best choice for Li intercalation and diffusion as potential anode materials, having the lowest intercalation energy and Li diffusion barrier, both of which are expected to result in better battery performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9S_jQlhpOkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEaXCpBRB78A"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The rate-detg. process for electrochem. energy storage is largely detd. by ion transport occurring in the electrode materials.  Apart from decreasing the distance of ion diffusion, the enhancement of ionic mobility is crucial for ion transport.  Here, a localized electron enhanced ion transport mechanism to promote ion mobility for ultrafast energy storage is proposed.  Theor. calcns. and anal. reveal that highly localized electrons can be induced by intrinsic defects, and the migration barrier of ions can be obviously reduced.  Consistently, expt. results reveal that this mechanism leads to an enhancement of Li/Na ion diffusivity by two orders of magnitude.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based materials have been considered as the most promising anode materials for both sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs), owing to their good chem. stability, high elec. cond., and environmental benignity.  However, due to the large sizes of sodium and potassium ions, it is a great challenge to realize a carbon anode with high reversible capacity, long cycle life, and high rate capability.  Herein, by rational design, N-doped 3D mesoporous carbon nanosheets (N-CNS) are successfully synthesized, which can realize unprecedented electrochem. performance for both SIBs and PIBs.                         rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black Anatase Titania with Ultrafast Sodium-Storage Performances Stimulated by Oxygen Vacancies</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jun; Ding, Zhiying; Wang, Chao; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhang, Yan; Wang, Chiwei; Zou, Guoqiang; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9142-9151</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructured black anatase titania with oxygen vacancies (OVs) is efficiently obtained and employed as an anode in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) for the first time.  The incorporation of OVs into TiO2 is demonstrated to render considerably enhanced-rate performances, higher initial capacities, and an accelerated electrochem. activation process during cycling, derived from the boosted intrinsic elec. cond. and improved kinetics of Na uptake.  Bestowed with the integrated merits of OVs and shortened Na ion diffusion length in the nanostructure, black titania delivers a reversible specific capacity of 207.6 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, retains 99.1% over 500 cycles at 1 C stably, and still maintains 91.2 mAh g-1 even at the high rate of 20 C.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. suggest that the lower sodiation energy barrier of anatase with OVs enables a more favorable Na intercalation into black anatase.  Thus, it is of great significance to introduce OVs into TiO2 to stimulate ultrafast and durable sodium-storage properties, which also offers a potential strategy to project more superior electrodes, utilizing internal defects.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeNB2DNlZ-6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhEaXCpBRB78A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XkslGqurk%253D&amp;md5=c2728c892db0db3c8cee72411e26f7f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1016/s0167-5729(02)00100-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Diebold, U.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Surface Science of Titanium Dioxide</span>. <i>Surf. Sci. Rep.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2003</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>48</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">53</span>â <span class="NLM_lpage">229</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/s0167-5729(02)00100-0</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The surface science of titanium dioxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Diebold, Ulrike</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Surface Science Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2003</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5-8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">53-229</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSREDI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-5729</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  TiO2 is the most investigated single-cryst. system in the surface science of metal oxides, and the literature on rutile (1 1 0), (1 0 0), (0 0 1), and anatase surfaces is discussed.  This paper starts with a summary of the wide variety of tech. fields where TiO2 is of importance.  The bulk structure and bulk defects (as far as relevant to the surface properties) are briefly reviewed.  Rules to predict stable oxide surfaces are exemplified on rutile (1 1 0).  The surface structure of rutile (1 1 0) is discussed in some detail.  Theor. predicted and exptl. detd. relaxations of surface geometries are compared, and defects (step edge orientations, point and line defects, impurities, surface manifestations of crystallog. shear planes-CSPs) are discussed, as well as the image contrast in scanning tunneling microscopy (STM).  The controversy about the correct model for the (1Ã2) reconstruction appears to be settled.  Different surface prepn. methods, such as reoxidn. of reduced crystals, can cause a drastic effect on surface geometries and morphol., and recommendations for prepg. different TiO2(1 1 0) surfaces are given.  The structure of the TiO2(1 0 0)-(1Ã1) surface is discussed and the proposed models for the (1Ã3) reconstruction are critically reviewed.  Very recent results on anatase (1 0 0) and (1 0 1) surfaces are included.  The electronic structure of stoichiometric TiO2 surfaces is now well understood.  Surface defects can be detected with a variety of surface spectroscopies.  The vibrational structure is dominated by strong Fuchs-Kliewer phonons, and high-resoln. electron energy loss spectra often need to be deconvoluted to render useful information about adsorbed mols.  The growth of metals (Li, Na, K, Cs, Ca, Al, Ti, V, Nb, Cr, Mo, Mn, Fe, Co, Rh, Ir, Ni, Pd, Pt, Cu, Ag, Au) as well as some metal oxides on TiO2 is reviewed.  The tendency to wet' the overlayer, the growth morphol., the epitaxial relationship, and the strength of the interfacial oxidn./redn. reaction all follow clear trends across the periodic table, with the reactivity of the overlayer metal towards O being the most decisive factor.  Alkali atoms form ordered superstructures at low coverages.  Recent progress in understanding the surface structure of metals in the strong-metal support interaction' (SMSI) state is summarized.Literature is reviewed on the adsorption and reaction of a wide variety of inorg. mols. (H2, O2, H2O, CO, CO2, N2, NH3, NOx, sulfur- and halogen-contg. mols., rare gases) as well as org. mols. (carboxylic acids, alcs., aldehydes and ketones, alkynes, pyridine and its derivates, silanes, Me halides).  The application of TiO2-based systems in photo-active devices is discussed, and the results on UHV-based photocatalytic studies are summarized.  The review ends with a brief conclusion and outlook of TiO2-based surface science for the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3ORpC9Y7lsbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhn_IayzKkRnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3sXivVWqtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=105db7a87a360e2042de551c7a4a05fc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1039/d0cc03099f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability of Dual-Ion Batteries Enabled by TiO<sub>2</sub> Microspheres with Abundant Oxygen Vacancies</span>. <i>Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Favorable effects of oxygen vacancies in TiO2-x synthesized via a calcination method on the electrochem. performance of dual Mg/Li-ion batteries are investigated.  The dual-ion cell shows excellent rate capabilities up to 40 C and outstanding cyclability up to 2500 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeDY0ui-MzJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhn_IayzKkRnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFOru7zJ&amp;md5=393fe76b8e39694e3bdd4c6e4abfa046</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c04481"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Pseudocapacitance Boosts Ultrafast, High-Capacity Sodium Storage of 3D Graphene Foam-Encapsulated TiO<sub>2</sub> Architecture</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsami.0c04481</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Pseudocapacitance Boosts Ultrafast, High-Capacity Sodium Storage of 3D Graphene Foam-Encapsulated TiO2 Architecture</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Rui; Ma, Yitian; Qu, Wenjie; Qian, Ji; Li, Li; Wu, Feng; Chen, RenJie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is an attractive anode for Li-ion batteries and Na-ion batteries because of its structural stability.  However, the electrochem. capability of anatase TiO2 is unsatisfactory due to its intrinsically low elec. cond. and poor ion diffusivity at the electrode/electrolyte interface.  We prepd. 3D lightwt. graphene aerogel-encapsulated anatase TiO2, which exhibits a high reversible capacity (390 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), a superior rate performance (164.9 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1), and a long-term cycling capability (capacity retention of 86.8% after 7800 cycles).  The major energy-storage mechanism is surface capacitance dominated, which favors a high capacity and fast Na+ uptake.  The inherent features of 3D porous aerogels provide addnl. active reaction sites and facilitate fast charge diffusion and easy ion access.  This will enable the development of 3D interconnected, graphene-based, high-capacity active materials for the development of next-generation energy-storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoA9imc5cibIrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhn_IayzKkRnA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosF2ntbo%253D&amp;md5=ff018a44946f3129ecf1da2a84ec5b86</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Augustyn, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Come, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lowe, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
